Fleischman Foundation\n\nSUIPR Report No. 648\n\ni6\nFebruary 1976\n\n.,y;\n\nInstitute for Plasma Research\nStanford University\nStanford, California\n\ni!Ul 108\n\ni gy\nGR.\xe2\x80\xa2\xe2\x80\xa2...... .\n\n,\n\n.^Ai+.4ll.fP^lfTr\n\nCG^E$\n\n^\t\n\n1\n\nInterplanetary Sector Structure 1947-1975\n\nby\n\nLeif Svalgaard\nInstitute for Piasma Research\nStanford University\n\nStanford, California 94305\nAbstract\nThis report is an extension of "An Atlas of Interplanetary\nSector Structure 1957-1974" to include earlier years back to 1947\nand also the years 1932 - 1933 and 1975.\n\ni^\n\nInterplanetary Sector Structure 1947-1975\n\nby\nLeif Svalgaard\nInstitute for Plasma Research\nStanford University\nStanford, California 94305\n\nThe present report is an extension of "An Atlas of Interplanetary\nSector Structure 1957-1974" (Svaigaard, 1975a), Using ground-based magnetograms from high-latituOe stations, the polarity of the interplanetary\nmagnetic field has been inferred for each day in the time period 1947-1958.\nDuring this interval stations within the polar caps were Operating most\nof the time malting reliable determination of the sector polarity possible.\nWe refer to the "Atlas" for details about the determinations and about\nthe representation of the data.\nExcept for about a year (August 1952 - September 1953) at least\none central polar cap station was always available. This means that the\naccuracy of the inferred polarities is high (m85% correct) and that for\nmany statistical investigations the inferred polarity is an adequate sub-\n\nE\t\nx`\t\n\nstitute for in-situ spacecraft observations (Wilcox et al., 1975; Russell\net al., 1975). During the time when only the polar cap boundary station\nGodhavn was operating, the sector structure was simple and stable. We\ntherefore believe that also during that interval the inferred polarity is\nof sufficiently high accuracy.\nThe data sources are shown on the data complilation sheets by code\nletters as detailed in the "Atlas". A few additional data sources are\ngiven below.\nG: Inferred by the author from Godhavn H which has a scale\nvalue of 9.5 nT/mm. The inference has been carried out\nrecently with no reference to earlier inferences,\n2\n\nD:\t\n\nInferred by the author from Dumont D\'Urville X. These\ninferences agree with the simultaneous Godhavn inferences\n75% of the time. If the probability that Godhavn and Dumont\nU\'Urville both agree is called q and if p denotes the probability\nthat Godhavn (or Dumont D\'Urville) agrees with the interplanetary\nsector polarity, then we have q - 1 - 2p(1-p). This ,.\np W\n\n0.85 for q = 0.75 attesting to the high accuracy of the\n\nGodhavn and Dumont D\'Urville inferences.\nJ:\t\n\nObjective determination of the polarity using Godhavn H.\nThe method is described in Svalgaard (1975b).\n\nN:\t\n\nYet another subjective inference by the author using Godhavn H\nand published by Antonucci (1974).\n\nSources J and N were only available for periods of a year each and\nwere included in the complilation to show hcw stable the inferences are\nwhen repeated.\nWe present in this report the following tables and data compilations:\n1)\n\nDaily classification of sector polarity 1947-1975.\n\n2)\n\nSector boundary list 1947-1975.\n\n3 ]\t\n\nBartels rotation plots of adopted sector structure 1947-1975.\n\n4\t\n\nData compilation sheets 1932-1933, 1947-1974.\n\n3\ns\'\n\nAcknowledgements\n\nThis work was supported in part by the Office of Naval Research\nunder contract N00014-76-C-0207, by the National Aeronautics and Space\nAdministration under Grant NGR 05-020-559,\t\n\nby the Atmospheric Sciences\n\nSection of the National Science Foundation under Grant ATH74-19007 and\nGrant DES75 -15664 and the xax C.
